### Added (S-0101 — cleanup-batch session: Issue #52 soft-warn category re-classification audit)

- **Validator-pipeline classification map** in [`engine/operations/tools-validate-interpretation.md`](operations/tools-validate-interpretation.md) — new top-level section between "Soft-warns (signal, not blocker)" and "Informational-only-accepted classifications". Comprehensive Markdown table covering all 40 soft-warn categories `validate.py` emits (38 static `r.soft_warn(...)` call sites + 2 dynamic-emission via the probe loop at `validate.py:687`). Each row: category → bucket → fire-rate over cadence-20 window (S-0081 → S-0100) → fire-rate over full 100-archive corpus → commits since 2026-04-25 → invariant guarded / role. Five buckets: Actively-tracked (default), Persistent-warn annotation, Informational-only-accepted, Actively-tracked deferred re-audit, Retire-candidate flagged for next audit. Threshold matrix documented inline as the calibration baseline subject to future tuning under [ADR 0042](adr/0042-soft-warn-lifecycle-archive-canon.md)'s amendment discipline. Re-run methodology (3-line python for fire-rate + 1-line `git log --grep` for acted-on rate) documented inline so the next cadence audit (S-0117 projected) reproduces without a permanent helper tool. Closes [Issue #52](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/52) — Non-obvious finding A from [`docs/health-checks/S-0097.md`](../docs/health-checks/S-0097.md).
- **"Actively-tracked, deferred re-audit" sub-section** in the same file — five entries: `timestamp_helper_bypass` (S-0095, ~5 archives coverage); `outcome_summary_unhandled_defer`, `next_session_handle_unknown_issue`, `next_session_handle_unknown_session`, `next_session_handle_malformed` (all S-0100, single-archive coverage). Each carries an explicit S-0117 re-classification trigger once ≥10 archives accumulate.
- **"Retire candidates flagged for next health-check audit" sub-section** in the same file — currently empty. Documents the S-0101 sweep's 0-finding result with the invariant-cover analysis: the 23 silent-in-cadence-window categories cluster into 7 invariant families (cascade discipline, graph audit per ADR 0016, MemPalace shared-state per ADR 0045 / ADR 0056, cross-reference integrity, format checks, phase-staged file expectations, routine-mode protocol per ADR 0051, ADR 0049 scope discipline, dynamic-emission probe failures). Two ghost archive keys excluded by design: `graph_audit_skipped` (an `add_check`, not a soft_warn) and `mempalace_diary_write_skipped` (a hard-fail, not a soft-warn).

### Added (S-0100 — cleanup-batch session: Issue #54 `next_session_handle` structured-field requirement)

- **`next_session_handle: str | None` field on [`engine/session/current.json`](session/current.json) and the archive** per [ADR 0049 Decision 6 (S-0100 amendment)](adr/0049-scope-lock-at-boot-and-descope-reorder-audit-at-shutdown.md) / [Issue #54](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/54). Closes Pushback Cluster A from the S-0097 audit (canonical instances S-0071 "correctable in any future session via a JSON edit" and S-0048 "preserved for manual review", both captured as `[pushback]`-prefixed drawers in `paideia/problems`). Initialized `null` at eager-claim per the lifecycle doc + Skill mirror. Filled at shutdown step 7b (new step) when `outcome_summary` carries hedge-pattern phrasing about deferred work. Three valid values: `"#<num>"` (Issue), `"S-<NNNN>"` (session, 4-digit), `null` (explicit "no defer" when hedge phrasing is intentional forward-pointer prose).
- **`validate_outcome_summary_unhandled_defer()` in [`engine/tools/validate.py`](tools/validate.py)** — new function gated to `--final-check` (alongside `validate_mempalace_adoption()`). Reads `outcome_summary` + `next_session_handle` from `current.json`; mid-session safety (skips when `outcome_summary` is null). Hedge regex set: 7 patterns (`future session`, `next session will`, `correctable in any`, `preserved for manual review`, `picked up by`, `defer indefinitely`, `revisit when`); case-insensitive, whitespace-tolerant; conservative starting set per Issue #54 (expand if false negatives surface in first 5 sessions). Disposition table emits one of four soft-warn categories: `outcome_summary_unhandled_defer` (primary positive — handle key absent from JSON), `next_session_handle_unknown_issue` (Issue verified missing via best-effort offline-graceful `gh issue view --timeout 5s`; only definitive "Could not resolve to an Issue" / "no issue or pr" stderr fires it; gh-not-installed / network failure / auth issues / timeouts all suppress), `next_session_handle_unknown_session` (S-NNNN matches no archive AND not next-claim slot), `next_session_handle_malformed` (string doesn't match `^#\d+$` or `^S-\d{4}$`, or non-string non-null type). Full Layer 1 contract docstring per [ADR 0038](adr/0038-three-layer-expression-contract-for-ai-authored-code.md); Layer 3 cold-context review at shutdown returned zero contract-vs-code drift.
- **`str_or_null` shape token in [`engine/tools/audit_archive_structured_fields.py`](tools/audit_archive_structured_fields.py) `shape_check()`** — accepts None or str; other shape tokens still reject None as a placeholder. The new shape semantically encodes "field must be present, value may be the load-bearing null" — distinct from missing field (still hard-fails) and from other nullable fields (which currently reject null entirely).
- **`next_session_handle` row in `REQUIRED_ARCHIVE_FIELDS`** at the same file (`since_session: S-0100`, `shape: str_or_null`, `adr: ADR 0049 Decision 6 (S-0100 amendment)`). Audit pipeline auto-validates the new field via the existing parameterized `audit_one()` per the Issue #20 / ADR 0056 (S-0078) parameterization fix — no audit-logic changes needed.
- **[`engine/tools/test_validate_outcome_summary_unhandled_defer.py`](tools/test_validate_outcome_summary_unhandled_defer.py)** — new pytest module, 26 cases covering: absent-current safety, malformed-JSON safety, mid-session safety (outcome_summary null / empty), no-hedge clean, hedge + handle-absent positive case, hedge + explicit-null suppression, hedge + Issue-verified-exists / not-found / gh-unavailable / timeout / auth-error, hedge + session-archive-exists / matches-next-id / unknown, malformed-handle paths (string + non-string), parameterized coverage of all 7 hedge phrases + a case-insensitive match.
- **7 new pytests** in [`engine/tools/test_audit_archive_structured_fields.py`](tools/test_audit_archive_structured_fields.py): `TestStrOrNullShape` (3 cases against the new shape token), per-field hard-fail/pass behavior at S-0100 vintage (4 cases — absent / null / valid string / wrong type), plus updates to `test_required_fields_are_well_formed` and `test_applicable_fields_filters_by_session_vintage` (S-0050 / S-0078 / S-0100 vintages).

### Changed (S-0099 — three Issue closures)

- **[`engine/tools/hooks/session-start.sh`](tools/hooks/session-start.sh) env-pointer probe** at lines 247-308 extended with parent-repo fallback for worktree-launched sessions. Inside a worktree, `REPO_ROOT` (= `git rev-parse --show-toplevel`) resolves to the worktree path, and `.env` is gitignored so it does not propagate to worktrees — the pre-S-0099 probe was checking the worktree's (absent) `.env` and emitting the LOUD onboarding pointer on every worktree-launched session even when the parent main repo's `.env` carried `SUPABASE_DB_URL` correctly. The fallback uses `git rev-parse --git-common-dir` (returns `/<parent>/.git` from inside a worktree; returns `$REPO_ROOT/.git` from a non-worktree session — same path, idempotent) + `dirname` to resolve the parent repo path; checks `<parent>/.env` for the URL line when the worktree's own `.env` is absent or lacks the URL. Original Issue #7 / S-0048 contract preserved: LOUD pointer still fires when neither location carries the URL. Verified empirically from the `pedantic-grothendieck-e50b33` worktree (parent has `.env+URL`, worktree has none): the LOUD block no longer fires.
- **[`engine/tools/health_check.py`](tools/health_check.py) `audit_mempalace()`** pushback/lesson counter loop at lines 1140-1193 extended with a content-prefix matching path. Drawers whose body has a line starting with `[<tag>]` (case-insensitive, optional leading whitespace) now count alongside drawers carrying the convention as a `Tags:` line value. A block matching BOTH forms counts once (deduplicated by block index). Surfaced by S-0097 audit's freshness probe: 3 substantive `[pushback]`-prefixed drawers in `paideia/problems` (S-0005, S-0048, S-0071) were reporting as 0 because the pre-S-0099 counter only matched `Tags:` line values. Bifurcated storage clarification landed at S-0098 in `engine/operations/mempalace-tagging-conventions.md` per Fit-1 adjudication; this is the script-side counterpart so the mechanical count reflects the bifurcated reality. Reported metric now includes a breakdown for trend visibility: `pushback-tagged drawers in MemPalace: N confirmed (via Tags-line match: K; via [pushback]-content-prefix match: M; deduplicated)`.
- **[`engine/tools/health_check.py`](tools/health_check.py) `audit_gaps()`** at line 673 now folds `audit_orphan_ok_list()` findings into its observations before the no-findings fallback. The orphan-OK audit is a gap-class concern per cascade-discipline.md framing.

- **[`engine/operations/health-check.md`](operations/health-check.md)** cadence-policy section extended with the S-0097 raise note alongside the existing S-0033 tightening note.
- **[`engine/build_readiness/adversarial_stance_first_exercise.md`](build_readiness/adversarial_stance_first_exercise.md)** Status: CLOSED. T1-A through T1-E all resolved at S-0097 with closure observations citing audit-report sections; ADR 0057 contract held — no ADR-warranting structural changes from first exercise. Two refinement-class observations (Non-obvious findings A and B in the audit report) route through User adjudication; both are documentation-class or category-re-class scope, not contract-amending.

### Added (S-0096 — issue close-out campaign C7: PDF input adapter, Issue #34)

- **`PDFInputAdapter` in [`engine/tools/parse_structural_reference.py`](tools/parse_structural_reference.py)** closes [Issue #34](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/34) per [ADR 0047](adr/0047-structural-reference-parser-tool-and-adversarial-triage-workflow.md) decision 6. Source-agnostic posture per ADR 0047 decision 1: no per-source code branches; multi-fallback at every detector. Title from `/Title` metadata (with junk-filter rejecting empty / digit-only / filename-shaped values) → first-page-largest-font fallback. Heading from pypdfium2 outline tree (non-recursive — pdfminer's recursive `get_outlines` blows the default 1000-deep recursion limit on Routledge's 2041 outline entries) → font-size buckets sampled within `PDF_FONT_SAMPLE_PAGE_COUNT` and emitted within `PDF_FONT_EMIT_PAGE_CAP` → `Chapter|Section|Part|Article` text-pattern with ≤8-word + ≤80-char + prose-connector-reject filters. Anchor from link annotations PLUS textual editorial markers (`See:`, `See also:`, `(see X)`, `→`, `Cf.`) — both paths emit canonical `internal:<slug>` hrefs picked up by one new universal pattern in `ENCYCLOPEDIA_CONFIG["cross_reference_patterns"]`. Slug-quality filter rejects pure-numeric slugs and editorial-positional references (`above` / `below` / `ibid`). Bulk text extraction via pypdfium2 (~30× faster than pdfplumber's pdfminer backend at encyclopedia scale). Image-only PDFs raise `ValueError` loudly. Paragraph and list-item element kinds NOT collected — no downstream detector consumes them.
- **Multi-entry partitioning in `extract_entries()`** per the docstring's "future" note: `partition_at_entry_boundaries(adapter_output, config)` splits the elements list at level-1 heading boundaries; `extract_entry_from_partition()` runs the existing detector pipeline against a scoped element list. Single-`<h1>` HTML still yields exactly one Entry — the 6 SEP fixture integration tests at `TestSEPFixtureIntegration` pass unchanged (load-bearing regression bar). Full-volume PDFs yield N Entries (Routledge: 2041).
- **Element reorder pass** (`PDFInputAdapter._reorder_elements_by_full_text_offset`): after PDF emission, sort elements by their first-occurrence offset in `full_text` so anchor-emission and heading-emission phases don't write disjoint position ranges that concentrate all cross-references into the LAST entry of any multi-entry brief. Headings positioned via `full_text.find` with monotonically advancing pointer for consecutive entries in document order; anchors carry `match.start()` as a private `_text_offset` attribute (stripped from the public surface after sorting). Result: Routledge's 10,512 cross-refs distribute across 1,177 of 2,041 entries (58%) with mean confidence 0.62.
- **Tests** (19 new): `TestPDFInputAdapter` (11 cases) exercises each fallback layer against `reportlab`-synthesized PDF fixtures — reportlab is added to `engine/tools/requirements.txt` as a test-only dep so no third-party PDF blobs land in git, keeping the [ADR 0011](../product/adr/0011-no-hosted-copyrighted-material.md) / [ADR 0046](../product/adr/0046-structural-reference-posture-extends-to-philosophy-reference-works.md) licensing posture clean. `TestMultiEntryPartitioning` (8 cases) exercises the partition logic directly including the per-partition cross-reference distribution regression bar. All 100 tests pass; ruff check + ruff format + mypy --strict clean.
- **Three-source convergence** at the C7 landing (validated against PDFs at `~/Documents/Claude_Files/temp/`, never copied into the repo): Routledge **2041 entries** with 58% carrying cross-refs (the architecture's strong case); Cambridge 20 entries and Oxford 15 entries (sparse — outlines enumerate book / letter sections only and entries are at body font size). The page-header-as-entry-indicator path that closes the Cambridge / Oxford gap is filed as [Issue #48](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/48) — source-agnostic in shape (universal first-line-of-page detection) but architecturally distinct from the outline + font-size + text-pattern stack landed here.

### Changed (S-0096 — `extract_entries` extension, ENCYCLOPEDIA_CONFIG, requirements.txt, ADR 0047)

- **`extract_entries()` rewritten** to partition-then-detect: previously single-Entry per AdapterOutput, now returns N entries via the partition orchestrator. Backward-compat preserved by the partitioner's no-boundary fallback (entire elements list becomes one partition when no level-1 headings present).
- **`ENCYCLOPEDIA_CONFIG["cross_reference_patterns"]` gains** one universal pattern `r"^internal:([a-z0-9][a-z0-9\-]*)$"` matching the canonical href form `PDFInputAdapter` emits. Existing SEP- and IEP-specific HTML patterns stay (HTML adapters' anchor hrefs still match them); the new pattern is appended last so the more-specific HTML patterns win when an HTML href happens to be slug-shaped.
- **`engine/tools/requirements.txt`** gains `pdfplumber>=0.11.0` (structural metadata: outline / chars / annotations / metadata), `pypdfium2>=4.0.0` (bulk text extraction; pinned explicitly even though pdfplumber re-exposes it transitively, so the version is independent of pdfplumber's pin), and `reportlab>=4.0.0` (test-only — `TestPDFInputAdapter` synthesizes PDF fixtures in-test).
- **[ADR 0047](adr/0047-structural-reference-parser-tool-and-adversarial-triage-workflow.md)** Consequences amended in-place with the C7 landing record: source-agnostic implementation rationale, multi-fallback layer descriptions, the pypdfium2-vs-pdfplumber split (text vs structural metadata), the multi-entry partitioning extension, the element-reorder pass, the three-source convergence outcome, and the Issue #48 forward-pointer for the page-header-entry-indicator path.

### Added (S-0095 — issue close-out campaign C6: timestamp standardization, Issue #33)

- **[ADR 0058 — Canonical timestamp format and shared timestamps.py helper](adr/0058-canonical-timestamp-format-and-helper.md)** closes [Issue #33](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/33). Six-element contract: (a) canonical `%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ` UTC second-precision Z-suffix, (b) all Python emission/parsing in `engine/tools/**/*.py` routes through `engine/tools/timestamps.py` (`emit` / `emit_micros` / `parse` / `today`), (c) `parse()` is tolerant of legacy `+00:00` shapes indefinitely (one-way back-compat per [ADR 0042](adr/0042-soft-warn-lifecycle-archive-canon.md) archive-as-canon), (d) hooks emit canonical via `date -u`, (e) four files allowlisted with rationale (`apply_migration.py` / `probe_push_gate.py` / `audit_mempalace_attribution.py` / `scan_mempalace_citations.py`), (f) non-goal: `time.time()` stopwatch math out of scope.
- **[`engine/tools/timestamps.py`](tools/timestamps.py)** — 4-function helper with full Layer 1 contract docstrings per [ADR 0038](adr/0038-expression-contract-for-ai-authored-code.md). `emit() -> str` canonical second-precision; `emit_micros() -> str` microsecond variant for one validator-telemetry call site; `parse(s) -> datetime` tolerant of canonical Z, `+00:00` (with or without microseconds), and the compact-time `%Y%m%dT%H%M%SZ` shape; `today() -> str` UTC date-only for day-of-event display surfaces (distinct from event-time emission).
- **[`engine/operations/timestamp-discipline.md`](operations/timestamp-discipline.md)** — Layer 1 source-of-truth doc, adjunct to [`code-discipline.md`](operations/code-discipline.md). Sections: canonical format, helper API, emit-vs-parse boundary, hooks-stay-shell rationale, allowlists (4 entries with per-file rationale), non-goal (stopwatch math), mechanical enforcement, manual procedure for adding a new emit site.
- **`validate_timestamp_helper_bypass()` in [`engine/tools/validate.py`](tools/validate.py)** — new AST-walk soft-warn category `timestamp_helper_bypass`. Walks each `engine/tools/**/*.py` source with `ast`, fires per `Call` node whose `func.attr` is `isoformat` / `strftime` / `fromisoformat` outside the file-path allowlist (`_TIMESTAMP_HELPER_BYPASS_ALLOWLIST`); excludes `test_*.py` from the walk. Validator check count rises 30 → 31. Persistent firing per [`soft-warn-lifecycle.md`](operations/soft-warn-lifecycle.md) 3-of-5 surface signals new ad-hoc emission slipping in.
- **33 new pytests + 1 extension** — [`test_timestamps.py`](tools/test_timestamps.py) 20 cases (shape regex per function, parse tolerance across all 5 accepted shapes, garbage rejection, UTC-not-local for `today()` mocked across the date boundary); [`test_validate_timestamp_bypass.py`](tools/test_validate_timestamp_bypass.py) 13 cases (empty walk / clean tool / per-shape detection / multi-callsite line-number reporting / 2 allowlist tests / test-file exclusion / syntax-error tolerance / nested subdirectory walk / unrelated-attribute non-firing / non-Python file ignore); [`test_health_check.py`](tools/test_health_check.py) gains `test_audit_bloat_duration_trend_handles_legacy_plus_offset` verifying the smoking-gun fix parses both Z-suffix and legacy `+00:00` archive shapes. Full pytest run across `engine/tools/`: 980 pass.

### Added (S-0094 — issue close-out campaign C5: apply_migration empirical postcondition verification, Issue #23)

- **Layer 2.5 in [`engine/tools/apply_migration.py`](tools/apply_migration.py)** — three new public surfaces close [Issue #23](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/23). `parse_postcondition_assertions(sql_text) -> list[tuple[str, int]] | None` parses inline `-- Postcondition-Assertions:` block from the contract header (each line `--   <SELECT returning one integer> :: <expected integer>`). The block ends at the next contract section header (`-- Invariants:`, `-- Rollback:`, etc.) — the section-header terminator pattern (`NEXT_SECTION_HEADER_RE`) prevents reading past the assertions block into prose containing PostgreSQL `::` casts. Returns `None` for header-absent (sentinel), `[]` for empty block (explicit "no assertions"). `verify_postconditions(db_url, assertions) -> tuple[bool, list[str]]` runs each assertion against the live DB via `psycopg.connect(autocommit=True)`; returns ALL failures (not just first) for diagnostic clarity; treats zero rows / non-integer / multi-column returns as failures with descriptive messages. `verify_shape()` early-detects malformed assertion grammar at shape time (exit 2) so the migration never reaches the apply step. `main()` runs Layer 2.5 between `record_in_schema_migrations` and the final success print.
- **New exit code 8** — distinct in kind from exit 7 (recording fault). Code 7 = "we lost track of what we applied"; code 8 = "what we applied does not match the contract". Caller-side recovery: identify whether (a) the assertion SQL is wrong, (b) the prose `-- Postconditions:` block is wrong, or (c) the migration body silently misbehaved. **schema_migrations is recorded regardless of assertion outcome** — body has committed atomically; skipping the record means re-fire either refuses with exit 6 or FK-collides on now-existing rows. Documented in module docstring + ADR 0055 amendment + `migration-discipline.md` Layer 2.5.
- **All 15 Phase 5 seed migrations annotated** with `-- Postcondition-Assertions:` blocks in [`product/seed-graph/migrations/`](../product/seed-graph/migrations/). [`0060_seed_crossbridges_part1.sql`](../product/seed-graph/migrations/0060_seed_crossbridges_part1.sql) annotated first as the highest silent-skip risk (71 cross-domain edges depending on 14 prior-migration FKs, no ON CONFLICT). Other 14 via one-shot `/tmp/annotate_seeds.py` script (deleted post-run) copying the prose-declared integers from each migration's `-- Postconditions:` field into machine-readable form. Per CLAUDE.md `feedback_no_pilot_wait_and_see.md` (annotate-only-future migrations is a pilot — the mechanism never exercises against the real corpus until net-new authoring occurs).
- **23 new pytests** in [`engine/tools/test_apply_migration.py`](tools/test_apply_migration.py) under `TestPostconditionVerification`: parser grammar (header absent / empty block / well-formed / prose-skipping / next-section-header termination / non-integer rejected / empty-SELECT rejected); verifier semantics (empty list / all-pass / one-fail / multi-fail-all-reported / zero-rows / non-integer / SQL-error-propagates / connection-error-propagates); main integration (warn-on-missing / pass-full-success / fail-still-records / multi-failure-stderr / SQL-error-during-assertion → exit 3 / shape-time-rejection-for-malformed-block / scope_lock-unaffected). New helper `_make_psycopg_stub_with_fetchone_seq` returns different values per query so multi-assertion paths are exercisable. Full suite: 47 tests green.
- **First-exercise readiness note** at [`engine/build_readiness/apply_migration_postcondition_first_exercise.md`](build_readiness/apply_migration_postcondition_first_exercise.md) per [ADR 0053](adr/0053-mechanism-first-exercise-gate.md). Sibling to [`apply_migration_first_exercise.md`](build_readiness/apply_migration_first_exercise.md) (S-0064 wrapper-itself first exercise). T1-A pending — closes at next routine fire post-S-0094 OR next interactive `--force` re-apply of an annotated seed. T1-B through T1-E resolved at S-0094.

### Changed (S-0094 — ADR 0055 + ADR 0039 amendments + ops doc + Skill updates)

Side-effect-conditional: applies only to patterns whose authoring produces deployments mutating external systems. Currently scoped to SQL/migrations only; future infrastructure-as-code patterns inherit the framing. Records the half-step framing rationale (a post-deploy verifier sits between Layer 2's "before the artifact exists" and Layer 3's "after the session ends, against the artifact text"; conflating them would dilute both).

Documents grammar, exit-code semantics, why-record-anyway rationale, cross-reference to Layer 3, and the layer's complementarity with Layer 3 (assertions catch silent-skip drift; cold-review catches premise drift; both required). Layer 3 cold-review prompt step 3 added directing reviewers to verify assertion-vs-prose drift and to focus on premise drift Layer 2.5 cannot catch (e.g., structural claims like "all edges within-domain").

- **New tool [`engine/tools/mempalace_boot_search.py`](tools/mempalace_boot_search.py)** — boot-time orchestrator per [ADR 0056](adr/0056-mempalace-mechanical-adoption-checks.md) S-0093 amendment, closes [Issue #38](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/38). - **New tool [`engine/tools/scan_mempalace_citations.py`](tools/scan_mempalace_citations.py)** — sibling shutdown scanner per ADR 0056 S-0093 amendment, closes [Issue #39](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/39). Runs at shutdown step 8b (after diary write + outcome_summary fill). Scans three sources for citation patterns: `outcome_summary`, today's diary entry (via `tool_diary_read(agent_name="claude", last_n=3)` matched on date), git commit messages from `git log <eager-claim-sha>..HEAD --format=%B`. Three regex patterns: `DRAWER_ID_PATTERN` (`drawer_<wing>_<hash>`), `SESSION_ARCHIVE_PATTERN` (`per/from/at/in/see S-NNNN` and `S-NNNN's <noun>`), `TAG_NAMED_PATTERN` (`per pushback/lesson/decision drawer`). Per-source dedup; cross-source sums. Writes nested `mempalace_citations` block under existing `mempalace_activity` field — rides the existing `REQUIRED_ARCHIVE_FIELDS` row in `audit_archive_structured_fields.py` per Layer 4 parameterization, no new audit row.
- **New soft-warn category `mempalace_zero_citations_after_search`** in [`engine/tools/validate.py`](tools/validate.py) `validate_mempalace_adoption()`. Fires when `mempalace_activity.search_calls > 0 AND mempalace_activity.mempalace_citations.total == 0` — closed-loop check that retrieved drawers actually inform authored artifacts. Gated on session id ≥ S-0093 (pre-S-0093 archives lack the citations block by design and would fire spuriously). Body cites the S-0093 amendment + ADR 0042 lifecycle. Validator check count rises 17 → 18.
- **27 new pytests** in [`engine/tools/test_mempalace_boot_search.py`](tools/test_mempalace_boot_search.py) — formulation generation determinism, similarity-filter behavior, current_plan.md section write/upsert idempotency, JSONL telemetry shim shape, empty-result handling, substrate-unreachable handling, mode resolution.
- **27 new pytests** in [`engine/tools/test_scan_mempalace_citations.py`](tools/test_scan_mempalace_citations.py) — pattern coverage (three patterns × multiple match shapes), per-source dedup + cross-source sum, multi-source aggregation, empty-source handling, idempotency, edge cases (URL false-positive avoidance, non-string outcome_summary, missing diary).
- **6 new pytests** in [`engine/tools/test_validate_mempalace_adoption.py`](tools/test_validate_mempalace_adoption.py) under `TestZeroCitationsAfterSearch` — search-with-zero-citations fires, no-search-no-citations vacuous, search-with-citations no fire, missing block defensive, malformed block defensive, body names search_calls.
- **923 engine/tools tests pass; mypy --strict + ruff check + ruff format clean** across all touched files.

### Added (S-0092 — issue close-out campaign C3: historical full-encoded-path wings deep cleanup)

- **`engine/tools/prune_mempalace.py` `--audit-historical-paths --apply` path** wired (was previously report-only since S-0088). Closes [Issue #41](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/41) — 9 historical wings holding 37,634 inaccessible drawers across `mempalace_drawers` plus 67 closet entries in `mempalace_closets`. Apply path now fans deletes out by chromadb collection via the new helper `fetch_uuids_by_collection` (joins `embeddings` -> `segments` -> `collections`) — discovered as a load-bearing fix during the S-0092 first apply against live, where the original drawer-only delete left 67 closet rows surviving (closets carry the same `-Users-...` wing tag as their grouped drawers; `collection.delete` is collection-scoped).
- **New helper `fetch_uuids_by_collection`** in `prune_mempalace.py` — returns `dict[collection_name, list[uuid]]` so the apply path can target each collection explicitly. The two known target collections (`mempalace_drawers`, `mempalace_closets`) are deleted from; any other collection surfaces as a WARN note rather than a silent miss. `delete_drawers_by_uuid` gained an optional `collection` parameter (default `mempalace_drawers`) so the orphan-wings + mined-ops-docs callers stay backward-compatible.
- **New audit report** at [`engine/docs/audits/historical-wings-signal-probe-S-0092.md`](docs/audits/historical-wings-signal-probe-S-0092.md). Two-pass direct-sqlite signal probe across all 37,634 historical-wing drawers: aggregate query verified zero non-empty `tag`, zero non-empty `type`, all `added_by=mempalace`, all `room=general` — confirming the S-0086 R3 #40C "Recommend retire" hypothesis with a definitive count rather than extrapolation. Cleared the Phase 1 halt-and-escalate trigger for the bulk-delete.
- **Pre-flight backups** at `~/.mempalace/palace.S-0092-pre-c3` (550M, captured the full 47,298-drawer pre-cleanup state) and `~/.mempalace/palace.S-0092-pre-closet-cleanup` (captured the post-drawer-delete pre-closet-cleanup state). Both retained on-disk per the S-0084 + S-0088 backup discipline; rollback via atomic-rename swap if anomalies surface in subsequent sessions.
- 8 new pytests in [`engine/tools/test_prune_mempalace.py`](tools/test_prune_mempalace.py) — covers dry-run shape, apply-path deletion across both collections (canonical wings preserved), idempotency, the new helper enumerator, the new `fetch_uuids_by_collection` helper (multi-collection bucketing + empty-input short-circuit), CLI backup-dir gate, CLI happy path. 33 tests in the file; mypy --strict + ruff check + ruff format clean.
- [`engine/operations/mempalace-operations.md`](operations/mempalace-operations.md) Prune procedure section: the historical-paths mode is now described as full apply-path-capable (was "report-only" pre-S-0092); classifier table extended with the historical-paths apply contract; example invocations include the historical-paths apply form. The S-0086 cross-reference + the closet-collection discovery are both named.

### Changed (S-0092 — palace footprint after deep cleanup)

- **MemPalace footprint dropped 79.2%** from 47,298 -> 9,819 drawers (delta -37,479). Wing count dropped from 13 to 7 (paideia, wing_paideia, wing_claude, sessions, plus three short-form per-worktree wings: wing_4840fe, wing_236026, wing_83d301). All 9 historical full-encoded-path wings cleared end-to-end across both `mempalace_drawers` and `mempalace_closets`. The `mempalace_wing_count_growth` soft-warn (post-S-0088 informational threshold 60) sits comfortably below threshold post-cleanup.

### Changed (S-0091 — close the no-token-no-diary hard-fail in routine mode + LOUD body uniformity + pending-diary index)

- **New soft-warn category `mempalace_diary_write_skipped_routine`** in [`engine/tools/validate.py`](tools/validate.py) — fires when `mempalace_activity.diary_write_calls == 0` AND `outcome_summary` lacks the acknowledgement token AND `mode == "routine"`. Replaces the engine-mode-only `mempalace_diary_write_skipped` HARD-FAIL for routine sessions. Engine retains the hard-fail (asymmetry justified by the unattended-vs-interactive difference: engine has an immediate fix path; routine cannot be killed by intermittent MCP per user directive *"I don't want any hard failures of mempalace MCP access because that holds up the whole line of routine sessions"*). LOUD body: `⚠️ ROUTINE DIARY DEFERRED — DO NOT BURY THIS`. Side effect: appends to a new `engine/session/diary_pending_index.json`.
- **LOUD body uniformly across modes** for the four substrate-availability soft-warns (`mempalace_substrate_at_close`, `mempalace_diary_write_acknowledged_skip`, `mempalace_diary_write_skipped_substrate_intermittent`, `mempalace_diary_write_skipped_routine`). Drops the S-0089/S-0090 engine/routine LOUD-vs-standard differentiation. Per user pushback at S-0090 close: *"I have to know that happened clearly in the session text so that when I review I can reconnect MCP and tell the session to do their diary entry later."* Archive review is the routine-side visibility surface; the ⚠️ prefix costs nothing extra in routine archives while serving the "clearly in session text" requirement directly. `_build_substrate_unavailable_body` lost its `mode` parameter.
- **New pending-diary index** at [`engine/session/diary_pending_index.json`](session/diary_pending_index.json). Schema `{schema_version: 1, pending: [{session_id, closed_ts, reason, outcome_summary_excerpt, archive_path}]}`. Mutable, committed to git. New helper `_append_to_diary_pending_index` in `validate.py` is idempotent against re-runs in a single session and degrades gracefully (logs to stderr, does not crash) when the index is missing or malformed. Operational allowlist entry in [`engine/tools/check_routine_scope.py`](tools/check_routine_scope.py) so routine-mode commits can write to it regardless of the active task's `scope_lock.allowed_paths`.
- **Boot-time pending-diary surface** in [`engine/tools/hooks/session-start.sh`](tools/hooks/session-start.sh). Reads the index; emits a LOUD attention block listing the count + session IDs when non-empty. Appears at every boot until processed. Block points at the recovery procedure documentation.
- **Recovery procedure documented** in [`engine/operations/routine-mode-operations.md`](operations/routine-mode-operations.md) — new "Deferred diary recovery" section. Manual procedure: reconnect MCP, open interactive session, read each pending archive, author a diary entry from the structured fields (`outcome_summary` + `work_done` + `mempalace_activity`), call `mempalace_diary_write`, remove the index entry. No new slash command (deliberate scope limit).
- 8 new pytest cases in [`engine/tools/test_validate_mempalace_adoption.py`](tools/test_validate_mempalace_adoption.py) under `TestRoutineProtectionS0091` — covers routine soft-warn (no hard-fail), LOUD body, index append, idempotency, missing-index graceful, malformed-index graceful, token-present-routine-doesn't-fire-skipped-routine, diary-written-routine-doesn't-touch-index. 5 existing `TestSubstrateTokenTightening` tests updated for LOUD-uniform body assertions: `test_token_substrate_intermittent_routine_standard_body` → `..._routine_loud_body`; `test_routine_session_acknowledged_skip_uses_standard_body` → `..._uses_loud_body`; `test_substrate_at_close_routine_standard_body` → `..._routine_loud_body`; `test_no_diary_no_token_substrate_alive_hard_fails` → `test_engine_no_diary_no_token_substrate_alive_hard_fails` (engine-only assertion). 37 tests in the file; 855 tests in `engine/tools/`; all pass. mypy --strict clean.
- [`engine/adr/0056-mempalace-mechanical-adoption-checks.md`](adr/0056-mempalace-mechanical-adoption-checks.md) — **third Decision-history entry** (Amendment — S-0091) recording the routine-protection refinement. Cross-references the user pushback quote, the plan file, and the implementation files. Coverage table contrasts engine vs. routine across all five mempalace-availability paths post-S-0091.
- [`engine/operations/tools-validate-interpretation.md`](operations/tools-validate-interpretation.md) — `mempalace_diary_write_skipped` entry rewritten as engine-mode-only; new `mempalace_diary_write_skipped_routine` entry; the three substrate-availability soft-warn entries (`substrate_intermittent`, `acknowledged_skip`, `substrate_at_close`) updated to document the uniformly-LOUD body shape post-S-0091.
- [`engine/operations/mempalace-operations.md`](operations/mempalace-operations.md) — adoption-checks table extended with the new `mempalace_diary_write_skipped_routine` row plus all four substrate-availability rows; **Severity rationale** paragraph rewritten to articulate the engine-vs-routine asymmetry; **Token contract** paragraph extended with the S-0091 layer (no-token routine path doesn't need the token; engine retains the original hard-fail behavior).
- [`engine/operations/session-shutdown-sequence.md`](operations/session-shutdown-sequence.md) — `outcome_summary_soft_warns` known-categories block extended with the five mempalace-availability soft-warn keys; the trailing paragraph documents the new `mempalace_diary_write_skipped_routine` category and its side effect on `diary_pending_index.json`.

### Changed (S-0090 — routine-protection refinement of S-0089's MCP-availability tightening)

- **`mempalace_diary_write_skipped_invalid_token` HARD-FAIL converted to `mempalace_diary_write_skipped_substrate_intermittent` SOFT-WARN** in `validate.py --final-check`. Per user clarification at S-0089 close: *"It's easy for me to fix the MCP connection issue. Seems that Claude Desktop has to be periodically rebooted to keep that working. I just need to know when it happens. I don't want that to kill routine sessions running overnight or while I'm AFK though."* S-0089's hard-fail blocked the close when substrate was alive but token was present — the routine-killing scenario the user rules out. S-0090 converts to mode-aware soft-warn: engine LOUD ⚠️ "MCP INTERMITTENT — DO NOT BURY THIS"; routine standard one-line. Visibility preserved (engine operator sees the contradiction; routine archive review surfaces the warn); routines close cleanly even on intermittent MCP. The S-0087/S-0088 burial pattern remains structurally hard to repeat because the LOUD body for engine sessions surfaces the substrate-alive + token-present contradiction explicitly.
- 2 new pytest cases in [`engine/tools/test_validate_mempalace_adoption.py`](tools/test_validate_mempalace_adoption.py) (`test_token_substrate_intermittent_engine_loud_soft_warn` + `test_token_substrate_intermittent_routine_standard_body`) replace the prior `test_token_invalid_when_substrate_alive`. 29 tests in the file; all pass.
- [`engine/adr/0056-mempalace-mechanical-adoption-checks.md`](adr/0056-mempalace-mechanical-adoption-checks.md) — **Consequences amendment** at S-0090 recording the routine-protection refinement. Cross-references the user clarification quote.
- [`engine/operations/tools-validate-interpretation.md`](operations/tools-validate-interpretation.md) — `mempalace_diary_write_skipped_invalid_token` hard-fail entry removed; new `mempalace_diary_write_skipped_substrate_intermittent` soft-warn entry with mode-aware body documentation; `mempalace_diary_write_acknowledged_skip` entry's stale "token invalidated" sentence corrected to reflect S-0090's always-soft-warn-closure contract.
- [`engine/operations/mempalace-operations.md`](operations/mempalace-operations.md) — **Mechanical adoption checks** section's token-contract paragraph rewritten to document the S-0089 + S-0090 layered contract (token always downgrades to soft-warn; category depends on substrate state at close).

### Added (S-0089 — MCP-availability boot/close warning surfaces + escape-hatch token tightening)

- **Boot-time MCP-availability probe** in [`engine/tools/hooks/session-start.sh`](tools/hooks/session-start.sh) — runs `mempalace status` at every session boot; LOUD attention block when CLI is missing OR substrate fails. Same surface treatment as ADR 0045's hard-broken probe findings. Mode-uniform at boot (hook fires before `/start-engine` or `/start-routine`); LOUD shape ensures the user sees it at the earliest possible moment regardless of session type.
- **Close-time substrate probe** in `validate.py --final-check` via new helper `_check_mempalace_substrate_alive()`. Uses `python3 -m mempalace status` to bypass PATH issues (mirrors the existing ruff/mypy/pytest invocation pattern). New soft-warn category `mempalace_substrate_at_close` fires when substrate is unreachable, independent of diary-write state. **Mode-aware body:** engine sessions get LOUD ⚠️ "DO NOT BURY THIS" prefix; routine sessions get a one-line standard body. Surfaces broken substrate as its own signal so the user sees it at every close, not only when the acknowledgement token is used.
- **New hard-fail category `mempalace_diary_write_skipped_invalid_token`** — fires when the `mempalace_unavailable_acknowledged:` token is present in `outcome_summary` BUT `mempalace status` succeeds at close-time. The token claims substrate unavailable; reality contradicts; the diary skip is the AI burying a real failure (the S-0087 + S-0088 burial pattern). Blocks the close — forces the AI to either invoke `mempalace_diary_write` immediately (since MCP is live) or investigate the upstream MCP-load timing issue.
- 13 new pytest cases in [`engine/tools/test_validate_mempalace_adoption.py`](tools/test_validate_mempalace_adoption.py) covering: token-invalid-when-substrate-alive (hard-fail), token-valid-when-substrate-down (soft-warn), engine-LOUD-body, routine-standard-body, substrate-at-close fires independently of diary state, substrate-at-close silent when alive but check still registered, and the helper's subprocess-run mocking branches (zero exit, nonzero, missing CLI, timeout, `python3 -m mempalace` form). All 28 tests in the file pass.

### Changed (S-0089 — operations docs absorb the MCP-availability mechanism)

- [`engine/adr/0056-mempalace-mechanical-adoption-checks.md`](adr/0056-mempalace-mechanical-adoption-checks.md) — **Consequences amendment** recording the S-0089 tightening: boot probe + close probe + token-validity tightening + LOUD body for engine sessions. Names the burial pattern (S-0087 + S-0088 archives both used the token while substrate was actually live) and the user pushback that named the gap. Pattern: in-place amendment, no supersession.
- [`engine/operations/tools-validate-interpretation.md`](operations/tools-validate-interpretation.md) — registers the new `mempalace_diary_write_skipped_invalid_token` hard-fail category; expands `mempalace_diary_write_acknowledged_skip` documentation with the mode-aware LOUD/standard body distinction; new `mempalace_substrate_at_close` soft-warn entry.
- [`engine/operations/mempalace-operations.md`](operations/mempalace-operations.md) — **Maintenance probes** section gains the MCP-availability probe entry (paired with the existing HNSW divergence detection); **Mechanical adoption checks** section's acknowledgement-token escape-hatch paragraph extended with the S-0089 tightening rule.

### Added (S-0088 — Issue close-out campaign session C2: MemPalace cleanup execution + boot-time guardrails)

- [`engine/tools/prune_mempalace.py`](tools/prune_mempalace.py) — **MemPalace prune tool** per [Issue #40](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/40). Three modes: `--audit-mined-ops-docs` (delete S-0002-mined drawers in `paideia/general` + `paideia/operations`), `--audit-orphan-wings` (delete `wing_<6-hex>` per-worktree orphans), `--audit-historical-paths` (report-only enumeration; deletion deferred to C3 / S-0089 per [Issue #41](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/41)). Default dry-run; `--apply` mutates with mandatory `--backup-dir` (mirrors the [`mempalace_rebuild_hnsw.py`](tools/mempalace_rebuild_hnsw.py) Phase 0 backup discipline from S-0084). Direct chromadb `collection.delete(ids=...)`; sqlite-backed metadata enumeration (~2 s on 47 K-drawer palace).
- [`engine/tools/test_prune_mempalace.py`](tools/test_prune_mempalace.py) — coverage for classifier patterns (orphan-wing regex, historical-full-path regex, mined `added_by` exact match), each audit mode (dry-run + apply), CLI-level error paths (missing palace, missing backup-dir, failing backup), and post-apply state verification (canonical wings preserved, mined drawers deleted, `claude-s0002-manual` curated drawers preserved).
- **`mempalace_wing_count_growth` soft-warn** in [`engine/tools/validate.py`](tools/validate.py) per [Issue #46](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/46). Parses `[probe-palace] wings: N (total)` from `probe_palace.py` extension; emits soft-warn at ≥ informational threshold (Tier 1) or LOUD-attention soft-warn at ≥ loud threshold (Tier 2). Body cross-references Issues #1, #2, #40, #41 and discipline rule that thresholds may only be raised AFTER cleanup batch lands. Validator `check_count` rises 17 → 18.
- **Wing-count probe extension** in [`engine/tools/probe_palace.py`](tools/probe_palace.py) — adds `_count_wings()` that queries `chroma.sqlite3`'s `embedding_metadata` table directly (`COUNT(DISTINCT string_value) WHERE key='wing'`) and emits the canonical `[probe-palace] wings: N (total)` line on the healthy path. ChromaDB stores all drawers in two collections (`mempalace_drawers` + `mempalace_closets`) with `wing` carried as metadata, so `len(client.list_collections())` is structurally always 2 — distinct-wing query is the only accurate accumulation surface.
- **Audit-trail boot surface** in [`engine/tools/scan_issue_backlog.py`](tools/scan_issue_backlog.py) per [Issue #47](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/47). Emits a second FYI line `[session-start] Active health-check audits: N (M open recommendations).` followed by indented audit-report paths, when `health-check-finding`-labeled Issues are present. Audit cross-references extracted via the `engine/docs/audits/<file>.md` regex (URL and bare-relative-path forms). Issues with the label but no detectable audit ref still count toward M.
- **`wing_count_growth_thresholds` block** in [`engine/session/register_state.json`](session/register_state.json) — `{informational: 60, loud: 100}` plus `_history` companion mirroring the `health_check_cadence_history` shape. Threshold reader silently falls back to defaults on absent / malformed config; bootstrap entry attributes the values to S-0088 / Issue #46.

- [`engine/operations/mempalace-operations.md`](operations/mempalace-operations.md) — new **Maintenance probes** section grouping HNSW divergence detection with the new wing-count probe; new **Prune procedure** section documenting `prune_mempalace.py` invocations + classifier signals (DELETE / PRESERVE table) + post-prune verification + tag-weighted retention policy.

### Removed (S-0088 — MemPalace prune execution)

- **414 mined ops-doc drawers** in `paideia/general` + `paideia/operations` deleted via `prune_mempalace.py --audit-mined-ops-docs --apply`. Source files (`MISSION.md`, `learner-model.md`, `tensions.md`, `architecture.md`, `pedagogy.md`, etc.) already in version control; reading via `Read` is more efficient than retrieval. Pre-prune backup at `~/.mempalace/palace.S-0088-pre-prune`.
- **79 orphan-wing drawers across 51 `wing_<6-hex>` wings** deleted via `prune_mempalace.py --audit-orphan-wings --apply`. Auto-capture artifacts of the upstream wing-naming bug per [Issue #1](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/1) / [Issue #2](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/2); all `type=diary_entry` with no `decision`/`pushback`/`lesson` markers (audit's "Recommend retire" verdict). Intermediate post-mined backup at `~/.mempalace/palace.S-0088-post-mined`.
- **Net effect:** 493 drawers removed (47,683 → 47,190). Wing count 64 → 13. New `mempalace_wing_count_growth` soft-warn fired pre-prune (64 > informational threshold of 60), cleared post-prune (13 < 60). `mempalace repair-status` post-prune reports status OK (HNSW 47,204 / SQLite 47,072 within flush-lag tolerance). Closes [Issue #40](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/40) parts A and B; part C (40K+ historical full-encoded-path drawers across 9 wings) remains C3 / S-0089 scope per [Issue #41](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/41).

### Changed (S-0087 — Issue close-out campaign session C1: MemPalace audit contract foundation)

- [`engine/adr/0056-mempalace-mechanical-adoption-checks.md`](adr/0056-mempalace-mechanical-adoption-checks.md) — **Consequences amendment** recording the S-0086 adversarial-review scale-back verdict per [Issue #43](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/43) (R4). Names the retirement program (KG family, tunnels family, AAAK-for-project-drawers), confirms the four-layer mechanical adoption checks contract still applies to the now-scoped surface, declares the new `mempalace_retired_surface_used` soft-warn as defense-in-depth, and clarifies the rollup-shape extension (kg_calls + tunnel_calls named buckets). Pattern: in-place amendment, no supersession.
- [`engine/operations/mempalace-operations.md`](operations/mempalace-operations.md) "Project usage scope" — **tightened** per [Issue #43](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/43) (R5). New "Scope is scoped, not exploratory" preamble cross-referencing the S-0086 audit and the ADR 0056 amendment. "What this project does NOT use" section names KG / tunnels / AAAK-for-project as retired-at-S-0087 (versus the prior "doesn't currently use" framing) with explicit forward-fit reasoning per surface and `wing_claude` AAAK diary carve-out preserved. New "Detection-side defense" paragraph names the `mempalace_retired_surface_used` soft-warn as the load-bearing surface against scope regression. - [`engine/operations/mempalace-tagging-conventions.md`](operations/mempalace-tagging-conventions.md) — **room-targeting clarification** per [Issue #43](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/43) (R8). New paragraph at the end of the "Room-targeting conventions" section: "Tagging carries the meaning; room targeting is best-effort." Cites sample drawer `drawer_paideia_decisions_a3d64680e953450f011e582f` from the audit. Don't move drawers between rooms post-hoc; the tagging convention is what governs retrieval.
- [`engine/operations/health-check.md`](operations/health-check.md) — **"Forward-fit map" subsection added** to the "Audit posture" section as a sibling to "Fit posture" per [Issue #44](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/44) (R7). Specifies the dual-temporal-frame discipline (BOTH historical fit AND fit-to-CONTINUE) per the lesson captured in `paideia/lessons` at S-0086 close. Names per-system role taxonomy (Load-bearing forward / Candidate-among-substrates / No role) and maps state-needs to candidate substrates. The Fit posture below uses the forward-fit map as one of its inputs.
- [`docs/health-checks/TEMPLATE.md`](../docs/health-checks/TEMPLATE.md) — new **"Forward-fit map" required subsection** between "Operative diagnostic applied" and "Non-obvious finding(s)" per [Issue #44](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/44). Tabular shape: forward state need → system-under-audit role → alternative substrate. The dual-frame produces the most decisive recommendations when historical and forward signals point opposite directions.
- [`engine/operations/tools-validate-interpretation.md`](operations/tools-validate-interpretation.md) — five new entries: `mempalace_boot_query_skipped`, `mempalace_diary_read_skipped`, `mempalace_diary_write_acknowledged_skip`, `mempalace_retired_surface_used` (new at S-0087), and the `mempalace_diary_write_skipped` hard-fail entry (the four ADR 0056 categories were undocumented in this index pre-S-0087; the new category lands alongside its sibling documentation).
- [`engine/tools/scan_mempalace_activity.py`](tools/scan_mempalace_activity.py) — TOOL_KEY_MAP gains 10 new entries (5 KG tools → `kg_calls`; 5 tunnel tools → `tunnel_calls`); EMPTY_ROLLUP gains both fields. Tracking retired-surface invocations in named buckets (rather than `other_calls`) is the foundation for the `mempalace_retired_surface_used` soft-warn detection per ADR 0056 Consequences amendment.
- [`engine/tools/validate.py`](tools/validate.py) — `validate_mempalace_adoption()` gains the `mempalace_retired_surface_used` soft-warn category. Trigger: `mempalace_activity.kg_calls > 0` OR `tunnel_calls > 0`. Single soft-warn naming both call counts when both fire. Severity: soft-warn (not hard-fail; transition window admits edge-case calls). Participates in 3-of-5 persistent-warn surface per ADR 0042.
- 4 new pytest cases in [`engine/tools/test_scan_mempalace_activity.py`](tools/test_scan_mempalace_activity.py) covering KG-bucket / tunnel-bucket / mixed-bucket / unknown-tool-falls-into-other; 5 new pytest cases in [`engine/tools/test_validate_mempalace_adoption.py`](tools/test_validate_mempalace_adoption.py) covering kg-call-fires / tunnel-call-fires / both-fire-single-warn / zero-no-warn / legacy-archive-no-warn (all 156 pass).
- **MCP-side per-tool filtering investigation outcome (per [Issue #42](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/42)):** not feasible at the harness layer — the `.mcp.json` registers the full tool surface and per-tool filtering would require a custom MCP-server wrapper out of scope for this chunk. Retirement is therefore discipline-enforced via `mempalace-operations.md` "Project usage scope" + the new soft-warn detection.
- **Health-check audit deferral cost:** validator soft-warn `health_check_overdue` fires every session in the C1 → C7 campaign window (slots_since=10 at S-0087, climbing to 16 at S-0093). Acceptable per user direction — the cadence-fired audit (formal first-exercise of [ADR 0057](adr/0057-adversarial-stance-for-health-check-audits.md)) runs in a dedicated post-C7 session.

### Added (S-0086 — Issue close-out campaign session S-D: MemPalace adversarial review)

- [`engine/docs/audits/mempalace-adversarial-review-S-0086.md`](docs/audits/mempalace-adversarial-review-S-0086.md) — **adversarial review of MemPalace per [Issue #35](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/35).** First concrete application of [ADR 0057](adr/0057-adversarial-stance-for-health-check-audits.md)'s adversarial-stance posture (the formal first-exercise of ADR 0057 remains the cadence-fired audit at S-0087). **Verdict: scale back.** The audit weighs both fit-historically AND fit-to-CONTINUE (per user direction during plan-mode review): historical evidence (12 of 12 pre-S-0078 sessions S-0066→S-0077 had zero MemPalace calls; ADR 0056 mechanically forced ≥1 call/session post-S-0078) underdetermines forward fit because the forward-fit map is decisive — Phase 6 self-correction, Phase 7 teaching layer, Phase DEC.1 (OQ-DEC1-A/B/C/D), OQ-CONTEXT-COMPRESSION, and OQ-PEDAGOGY-INFERENCE-LOCUS all specify Postgres + pgvector + ephemeral in-session summarization with **zero MemPalace dependency in product runtime**, while ADR 0057's cadence-audit `pushback`/`lesson` substrate, ADR 0051's routine-mode boot diary read, two-layer decision recording, and engine-side cross-session pattern detection are **load-bearing forward**. The load-bearing core (decisions room: 72 drawers tracking 58 ADRs with substantive content; lessons: 117 concrete failure-mode recoveries; problems: 291 verbatim pushback moments; diary: 160 entries; well-targeted boot search returning 6/6 substantive content on substantive queries; hooks + probe per ADR 0045 + S-0084) earns its weight; the dead-weight perimeter (KG / tunnels / AAAK-for-project / 88 mined ops-doc drawers / 50+ orphaned per-worktree wings / 40K+ inaccessible historical full-encoded-path wings / `mempalace_status` protocol-message overhead) does not. Per ADR 0057 element 1 (user-buffered execution), the audit produces 8 numbered recommendations (R1–R8: implement Issues #38/#39/#40 with audit-specified scope expansion; small-scope ADR 0056 amendment recording the verdict; ops-doc and tagging-conventions updates) — execution work lands downstream after user adjudication. Cold-context probe target: ADR 0048 (random-pick from `find engine/operations engine/adr docs/health-checks engine/build_readiness -name '*.md' -type f`); read healthy with no drift.

### Changed (S-0086 — first concrete application of ADR 0057 framework)

- [`engine/session/current.json`](session/current.json) `declared_scope` field added at session boot per [ADR 0049](adr/0049-scope-lock-at-boot-and-descope-reorder-audit-at-shutdown.md), closing the `empty_declared_scope` soft-warn that surfaced at eager-claim. The S-0085 ENGINE_LOG entry recorded the same fix; the per-session need to add the field is a recurring authoring step tracked by the validator, not a structural defect.

### Added (S-0085 — Issue close-out campaign session S-C: health-check audit posture overhaul)

- [ADR 0057](adr/0057-adversarial-stance-for-health-check-audits.md) — **adversarial stance for project health-check audits.** Sibling to [ADR 0040](adr/0040-build-readiness-gate-before-substantive-build-sessions.md) (gate-side adversarial reconnaissance) at the cadence-audit endpoint. Closes [Issue #30](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/30) (adversarial-stance posture, structurally upstream of #28 and #36), [Issue #28](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/28) (freshness probes per external system; stats-as-proxy-for-function anti-pattern named), [Issue #36](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/36) (pushback/lesson drawer content reading + clustering at audit time). Five contract elements: (1) **user-buffered execution** — audit findings + guidance suggestions surfaced *before* any retire/convert/replace action; user adjudicates; downstream sessions execute via Issues per ADR 0048 (added per user pushback during plan-mode review: "The health checks adversarial stance needs to be buffered by reporting its findings and guidance suggestions to me before taking action"); (2) **posture inversion** — adversarial prompt-question rewrites for Fit/Gaps/Infrastructure-without-function/Bloat with recommendation-shape dispositions (`recommend retire / recommend convert / recommend preserve-with-affirmative-case`); (3) **stats-as-proxy-for-function** named anti-pattern — every system reference rests on a content probe run during the audit, not citations of cached stats; (4) **required output ≥1 affirmative retire-candidate-recommendation** (or adversarially-scrutinized explicit "no candidates" subsection); (5) **cold-context probe per audit** — read ≥1 randomly-selected artifact as if no project context. First-exercise gate per [ADR 0053](adr/0053-mechanism-first-exercise-gate.md); the cadence-fired audit at S-0087 is the first exercise.
- "Adversarial stance" section in [`engine/operations/health-check.md`](operations/health-check.md) carrying the user-buffered execution principle, stats-as-proxy anti-pattern, posture inversion principle, cold-context probe specification.
- "Mechanical inputs and freshness probes" section in [`engine/operations/health-check.md`](operations/health-check.md) (renamed from "Mechanical inputs"). Per-system freshness-probe inventory — MemPalace search-recall content quality, validator soft-warn acted-on rate (`git log --grep` per persistent category vs archive `outcome_summary_soft_warns` deltas), Supabase migration empirical postcondition, hook-log success-exit verification, register-content capture rate. Documents `health_check.py`'s existing `audit_mempalace()` `pushback`/`lesson` adoption-count probes as **canonical contract** (no code changes; the probes existed pre-S-0085 between S-0065 and S-0077 but were not documented as required).
- Adversarial prompt-questions in all four posture sections of [`engine/operations/health-check.md`](operations/health-check.md) — Fit ("what machinery is silently ignored…"), Gaps ("if a new collaborator joined the project tomorrow…"), Infrastructure-without-function ("argue this candidate's retirement"), Bloat ("if the project's machinery were forced to halve in size…"). Each posture also gains an "Argue retirement / replacement" sub-prompt. Disposition options for Infrastructure-without-function shift from `[retire / convert / preserve]` to `[recommend retire / recommend convert / recommend preserve-with-affirmative-case]` per the user-buffered execution principle.
- "Accumulated pushbacks and lessons" section in [`engine/operations/health-check.md`](operations/health-check.md) with concrete `mempalace_search` commands per [Issue #36](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/36). Audit AI reads `pushback`/`lesson` drawer *content* (not just count) since `last_audit_session`, surfaces clusters in prose, distinguishes "posture not exercised" from "capture surface failing silently" by sampling diary entries when zero captures appear.
- [`engine/build_readiness/adversarial_stance_first_exercise.md`](build_readiness/adversarial_stance_first_exercise.md) — first-exercise readiness note per [ADR 0053](adr/0053-mechanism-first-exercise-gate.md). Mechanism qualifies under criterion #4 (Consequences span 6 surfaces). T1-A through T1-E (drawer-content reading; user-adjudication-blank; freshness-probe content findings; random-pick procedure; ≥1 retire-candidate or adversarially-scrutinized "no candidates") pending the next cadence-fired audit (S-0087 by recommended sequencing). T2-A through T2-D and T3-A through T3-C documented for the first-exercise session to consume.

Each section's prompt-questions and disposition labels are recommendation-shape, not action-shape, per the user-buffered execution principle. Existing posture-prose preserved alongside the adversarial rewrites where load-bearing.

### Added (S-0084 — Issue close-out campaign session S-B: HNSW divergence detection + non-destructive restoration)

- [`engine/tools/probe_palace.py`](tools/probe_palace.py) — **divergence-detection extension per the [ADR 0045](adr/0045-shared-state-integrity-discipline.md) S-0084 amendment for [Issue #31](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/31).** The probe now shells out to upstream's `mempalace repair-status` subcommand (read-only by upstream contract; never opens a chromadb client) after the existing chromadb-openability check. Emits `[probe-palace] divergence: HNSW=N1 SQLite=N2 (P%)` on stderr when the upstream tool is available and parseable. Exit code promotes from 0 (healthy) to 1 (suspect) at ≥10% divergence; existing 2 (hard-broken) and 139 (segfault) paths unchanged. The `mempalace` binary being absent from PATH is a graceful skip — the divergence check returns None and the existing exit-code logic continues. Discovered during planning that the upstream tool already exists; building a probe from scratch was unnecessary reinvention.
- [`engine/tools/validate.py`](tools/validate.py) — **new soft-warn category `mempalace_hnsw_divergence`** in `validate_shared_state_health()`. Parses the divergence stderr line emitted by probe_palace.py and emits the soft-warn at ≥10% divergence with a body that names the percentage and the BM25-fallback consequence. At ≥30% divergence, the body adds the destructive-repair carve-out warning verbatim, naming the S-0078 forensic (99.7% loss observed) and pointing at the supported restoration path. Validator check count rises from 16 to 17.
- [`engine/tools/mempalace_rebuild_hnsw.py`](tools/mempalace_rebuild_hnsw.py) — **new tool: non-destructive HNSW rebuild that bypasses `mempalace repair --mode legacy`.** Reads `(embedding_id, document, metadata)` tuples directly from `chroma.sqlite3` via the METADATA-segment join (bypassing the chromadb get-with-embeddings path that fails on divergent palaces with `InternalError: Error finding id`). Deletes the collection preserving its metadata, recreates, and re-adds via `collection.add(ids, documents, metadatas)` WITHOUT explicit embeddings — chromadb re-computes via the registered embedding function and writes BOTH SQLite and HNSW segments fresh. Trade-off accepted: rebuilt vectors are not byte-identical to originals (the embedding function may have shifted across versions) — but the alternative is to permanently lose the divergent drawers' data, since their original vectors aren't present in the palace. CLI surface: `--palace <required>`, `--collection <repeatable>`, `--batch-size`, `--dry-run`, `--verify-only`, `--embedding-providers`. The `--embedding-providers` flag enables CoreML acceleration on Apple Silicon (50× speedup observed at S-0084 vs CPU-only); the providers override is process-local and doesn't pollute the persisted collection metadata. 5-tier exit-code semantics: 0 success / 1 extraction-short refusal / 2 mid-flight failure (collection deleted, re-add incomplete; restore from snapshot) / 3 post-verify divergence ≥1% / 4 non-default embedding function refusal / 5 generic pre-destructive error. 3 unit tests against synthetic chromadb fixtures.
- "Maintenance probes" section in [`engine/operations/health-check.md`](operations/health-check.md) documenting the divergence probe and the destructive-repair carve-out for audit-time consumers.
- "Known issues" entry in [`engine/operations/mempalace-operations.md`](operations/mempalace-operations.md) documenting the destructive-repair pattern, forensic detail, restoration path via the new tool, and atomic-rename swap procedure.
- New `mempalace_hnsw_divergence` category in [`engine/operations/tools-validate-interpretation.md`](operations/tools-validate-interpretation.md).
- 4 new pytest cases in [`engine/tools/test_probe_palace.py`](tools/test_probe_palace.py) covering: divergence-line emission with stub mempalace binary, exit-code promotion at ≥10%, graceful handling when mempalace is absent from PATH, negative-test that probe never invokes bare `mempalace repair`.
- New test file [`engine/tools/test_mempalace_rebuild_hnsw.py`](tools/test_mempalace_rebuild_hnsw.py) with 3 cases: round-trip count + metadata preservation, `--dry-run` writes nothing, refusal on non-default embedding function (per upstream Issue #1255).
- Upstream MemPalace bug filed: [MemPalace/mempalace#1394](https://github.com/MemPalace/mempalace/issues/1394) — destructive `mempalace repair --mode legacy` against the version installed at S-0078 wiped 99.7% of SQLite embedding rows; distinct from #1208's 10K cap pattern. Cross-references upstream Issues #1238, #1255, #1263, #1308, #1362, #1092 as adjacent.

### Changed (S-0083 — Issue close-out campaign session S-A: cleanup batch + ideation.md retire + tiktoken retire)
- [`engine/tools/scan_mempalace_activity.py`](tools/scan_mempalace_activity.py) — **bug fix per [Issue #37](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/37).** Now truncates `current_mempalace.jsonl` after writing the per-session rollup so subsequent sessions don't inherit prior-session calls. Pre-S-0083 the JSONL accumulated indefinitely — S-0082's `mempalace_activity.total_calls=7` reflected S-0081's 4 calls plus S-0082's 3. Truncation gated on the success path: if `current.json` is absent (rollup write fails), the JSONL is preserved intact for recovery. 4 new pytest cases.
- [`engine/build_readiness/README.md`](build_readiness/README.md) — **rewritten per [Issue #26](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/26).** Six file classes now indexed (gate reports, audit-warrant gate reports, audit master-plan reports, closeout reports, first-exercise readiness notes, apparatus-improvement retrospectives) with per-class authoring trigger / contract / consumer / index table. Cross-refs ADRs 0040 / 0051 / 0053 and operational docs build-readiness-gate.md / routine-mode-operations.md / mechanism-first-exercise-gate.md. Lifecycle and See-also sections updated. Closeout-class indexing (the issue's specific ask) lands as one of six classes rather than as a single section, since the audit-closeout future state will introduce additional classes anyway.

### Removed (S-0083 — `transcript_token_pct` telemetry retired per Issues #21 + #32)
- [`engine/tools/scan_context_telemetry.py`](tools/scan_context_telemetry.py) — **deleted** along with its 14 pytest cases at `engine/tools/test_scan_context_telemetry.py`. Empirical justification per Issue #32: the Session-load trend section consumed this telemetry across S-0052 / S-0065 / S-0077 audits and produced **zero behavioral signal** (S-0052 absorbed by triage of >1.0 fluke; S-0065 had 62% None capture rate filed as Issue #21; S-0077 produced "low and stable; no bundling-recommendation change"). The capture itself fluctuated non-deterministically across routine-mode sessions (Issue #21 reframed at S-0077). The defensive surface area required to keep the metric from being misread as live in-session pressure (Issue #11 inline-fix; CLAUDE.md "Posture vs machinery" bullets; the at-read-site cumulative-vs-live framing) outweighed the metric's contribution to actionable decisions.
- `tiktoken>=0.7.0` pin from [`engine/tools/requirements.txt`](tools/requirements.txt). chromadb and mempalace pins remain.
- Step 7b "Capture context telemetry" from [`engine/operations/session-shutdown-sequence.md`](operations/session-shutdown-sequence.md) and the corresponding step in [`.claude/skills/session-shutdown-sequence/SKILL.md`](../.claude/skills/session-shutdown-sequence/SKILL.md). Step 8 (outcome_summary fill) now follows step 7a (scope-delivery audit) directly.
- "Session-load trend" section from [`engine/operations/health-check.md`](operations/health-check.md) (both subsections). The cross-session "running too long / too short / high variance" analysis was the consumer that produced no behavioral signal.
- Two `transcript_token_pct` bullets from [`CLAUDE.md`](../CLAUDE.md) "Posture vs machinery" — the cumulative-vs-live distinction (Issue #11 closure) and the prior-archive-backstop rejection. The mid-session-context-pressure-monitoring bullet is preserved (the underlying gap remains; the operating policy of manual user monitoring is unchanged) but trimmed to remove tiktoken-specific framing.
- `Bash(python3 engine/tools/scan_context_telemetry.py:*)` from [`.claude/settings.json`](../.claude/settings.json) permissions allowlist.

### Removed (S-0083 — `product/docs/ideation.md` retired per Issue #29)
- `product/docs/ideation.md` — **deleted.** The file was empty (header rows only, no data rows) across S-0001 through S-0077. Its function (capture proposed work / ideas / aspirations) had structurally migrated to GitHub Issues with the `enhancement` label per [ADR 0048](adr/0048-handoff-narrowing-and-github-issues-for-cross-session-deferrals.md) (S-0042). Three consecutive audits (S-0052 / S-0065 / S-0077) preserved the file by reading the empty state as "correct shape" without testing whether the function had migrated — a load-bearing instance of the stats-as-proxy-for-function anti-pattern (Issue [#28](https://github.com/StarshipSuperjam/paideia/issues/28)). The S-0077 user feedback flagged the audit failure pattern; the user's S-0083 directive chose full retirement (option A in the issue body) over pointer-ify (option B).
- Inbound-reference cleanup spans 10 active sites: [`engine/tools/hooks/pre-commit`](tools/hooks/pre-commit) exploration-mode allowlist; [`engine/tools/scan_orphans.py`](tools/scan_orphans.py) `_REGISTER_FILE_NAMES`; [`engine/tools/health_check.py`](tools/health_check.py) `IDEATION_PATH` constant + the unconsumed-ideation-entries audit block (`audit_dead_weight()`); [`engine/tools/test_scan_orphans.py`](tools/test_scan_orphans.py) register-emptiness tests rewritten against `tensions.md`; [`engine/tools/test_health_check.py`](tools/test_health_check.py) ideation tests dropped + `synthetic_repo` fixture monkeypatch removed; [`engine/operations/health-check.md`](operations/health-check.md) `register-empty` axis description; [`engine/operations/session-shutdown-sequence.md`](operations/session-shutdown-sequence.md) capture-flow guidance redirected to GitHub Issues; [`.claude/skills/session-shutdown-sequence/SKILL.md`](../.claude/skills/session-shutdown-sequence/SKILL.md) mirror; [`README.md`](../README.md) project-structure diagram + pre-commit-hook description. Historical refs in [`HANDOFF.md`](../HANDOFF.md), [`engine/ENGINE_LOG.md`](ENGINE_LOG.md), archived `docs/health-checks/*`, and the S-0042 build_readiness retrospective are preserved unchanged per their respective lifecycles.

### Added (S-0082 — Phase 5 production audit master plan; T-PHASE-5-AUDIT routine target lands)
- [`engine/build_readiness/phase_5_production_audit.md`](build_readiness/phase_5_production_audit.md) — master-plan gate report for the Phase 5 graph production audit per S-0081 gate's PROCEED recommendation. Contents: scope/anti-scope, fixed SEP-anchored prompt template (per-edge + per-node, copy-paste-discipline rather than paraphrase to prevent AI-generic critique), fixed evidence file schema, sample-size policy table (35% per-subdomain density per S-0081 expansion rule given 47% cross-bridge defect rate; ~265 edges + ~96 nodes + 10 hubs reviewed across the 12 sessions), three diagnostic syllabus targets (Gettier counterexamples to JTB / modal realism / social_contract_theory — `social_contract_theory` substituted for absent `free_speech` per S-0081 coverage finding), Tier 1/2/3 triage (T1-A through T1-F resolved; T2-A through T2-E codified; T3-A through T3-F deferred to closeout), 4 pre-listed audit-system-input proposals (`edge_evidence_empty`, `discipline_label_node_at_root`, `prereq_direction_summary_inconsistency` (NLP-flagged, possibly defer), `historical_node_as_prereq_source`), structural-reopen pre-flag for `historical_influence` predicate activation (S-0081 extrapolation: ~19 of 71 cross-bridges historical-not-pedagogical exceeds the ≥10 ADR-warranting threshold), forward pointers to closeout (final reports, Issue filing, ADR memos, README multi-class restructure per Issue #26).

Per-task scope_lock pinned to single evidence file under `engine/build_readiness/phase_5_production_audit_evidence/<task>.md`; criteria are `file_exists` + `validate_passes`. Closeout (interactive) is NOT a target task — T1-F discipline. check_target.py parses cleanly: 12 tasks pending, validate_passes already true, file_exists pending evidence-session work.
